# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Graceful Shutdown Signal Handling Across Go Services

## Your Task

Find Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes, grafana/grafana, and prometheus/prometheus that handle SIGTERM/SIGINT for graceful shutdown: the signal handler registration, the shutdown timeout, and the cleanup ordering (drain connections before stopping goroutines).

## Context

## Available Resources

58-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of graceful shutdown signal handling across the three Go repositories. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **11 key files** and **7 critical symbols** that handle SIGTERM/SIGINT for graceful shutdown:

### **Kubernetes** - Most sophisticated graceful shutdown
- **Signal registration**: `signal.Notify()` with buffered channel to handle multiple signals
- **Shutdown sequence**: Defined lifecycle events (ShutdownInitiated → AfterShutdownDelayDuration → NotAcceptingNewRequest → InFlightRequestsDrained)
- **Timeouts**: 70-second delay before shutdown, 60-second timeout for draining requests
- **Drain ordering**: Explicitly waits for all in-flight requests to complete (InFlightRequestsDrained) before calling server.Shutdown()

### **Prometheus** - Actor-model coordination
- **Signal registration**: Simple signal.Notify() for SIGTERM/SIGINT and SIGHUP (reload)
- **Cleanup ordering**: Uses oklog/run.Group pattern - each goroutine has Execute() and interrupt() handlers
- **Structured shutdown**: When signal arrives, interrupt handlers are called in coordinated order to shut down notifier, TSDB, discovery managers

### **Grafana** - Context-based propagation
- **Signal registration**: Multiple operators register handlers in connection_operator, repo_operator, zanzana_folder_reconciler, jobs_operator
- **Shutdown timeout**: gRPC server has GracefulShutdownTimeout with fallback to Stop()
- **Cleanup ordering**: Context cancellation propagates to all background services; waits with timeout before returning

All three implement the key principle: **drain connections/complete in-flight work before stopping goroutines**.

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.
